Comments: 7. What most excites you about San Antonio's future? /¿Qué es lo que más lo emociona del futuro de San Antonio? [#144542]	"I'm really not sure. I see a lot of half-a**ed measures and forgotten plans. It seems like every 5-10 years we see a new ""initiative"" that is never developed or implemented meaningfully. There was the decade of San Antonio, which never really got off the ground, the ""five-regional-hubs"" that I haven't heard of since the survey, and now ""climate ready SA"". I think it would be better to focus on a few, well-defined initiatives and actually achieve them, than to focus on some golden broad futuristic plan that never gets off the ground because of infighting and lack of ability to drill down to the implementation phase. Pick one or two things, figure out how to measure the costs and benefits, do them really really well, and publish the data on the costs, benefits, and outcomes (honestly, not in some propaganda way), lessons learned, and then pick another couple of things, and build momentum that way. Stop wasting money on consultants whose reports say nothing concrete and have no actionable steps and put the money towards actually achieving something, even if it isn't the splashiest or even the best choice. Just do something. Then, do something else concrete. One step at a time. Lots of little actual improvements that build to something momentus over time. Quit ruminating and DO SOMETHING. Then tell us about it. The good, the bad, the ugly, the outstanding. Own your projects and results. Learn from your mistakes. We're all human. "

Comments: 7. What most excites you about San Antonio's future? /¿Qué es lo que más lo emociona del futuro de San Antonio? [#144542]	"In honesty, not too much. But I grew up here and my opinions are not championed because they do not drive a profit. 
I acknowledge the city has done a fantastic job revamping downtown and creating beautiful spaces for tourists but I'm saddened to see the exponential growth of gentrification and displacement of native San Antonians. Our downtown is being bought up by outsiders. While it is shiny and nice, I've noticed I feel less safe downtown now. The cost to come downtown for the day is ridiculous with sky high parking rates. I feel this will another way of segregating an already incredibly segregated city. 
I worry about the sustainability of this unchecked growth. I worry about our aquifer. I worry about the urban sprawl that has crept far beyond 1604 and has removed the natural beauty of our land. Everything is for sale for the right price now. 
What would excite me most about San Antonio is if we stopped to consider the harm being done now that will have an impact in seven generations."
